\l Those (ego's husband's or wife's siblings), if they are elder than oneself, one calls them a-pi `my elder sibling'; if they are younger one calls them a-ʁi `my younger sibling'. They also call each other a-xtɤɣ`my brother' and the like.' (140425 kWmdza05) <a href="https://doi.org/10.24397/pangloss-0003789"></fn>

\t kɤndʑimɤtsa nɯni tɕe ci kupandʑi kɯkʰɯ ɲɯŋu , kɯŋgrɤl ɲɯŋu , mɤkɯʁdɯɣ ɲɯŋu .
\g COLL-MZCh DEM:DU LNK one IPFV-make-DU INF:STAT-be.possible SENS-be INF:STAT-be.usually.the.case SENS-be NEG-INF:STAT-be.harmful SENS-be
\l For two maternal parallel cousins, it is possible to get married, it is the custom, it is not wrong.' (140427 kWmdza stWnmW)

\t kɤndʑiwɤmɯsnom ɯrɟit nɯ pɯpɯŋunɤ , ( . . .) ɯnɯni li ci kupandʑi kɯkʰɯ ɲɯŋu . tɕeri nɯnɯ ɲɯrkɯn .
\g COLL-brother-sister 3SG.POSS-offspring DEM TOP _ DEM:DU again one IPFV-make-DU INF:STAT-be.possible SENS-be LNK DEM SENS-be.rare
\l Cross-cousins (the children of siblings of different gender) can also get married, but it is rare.' (140427 kWmdza stWnmW)

\t kɤndʑixtɤɣ ɯrɟit nɯ tɤŋu tɕe tɕe , ci kúwɣpa maka mɤkɯkʰɯ ɲɯŋu .
\g COLL-brother 3SG.POSS-children DEM AOR-be LNK LNK one IPFV-INV-make at.all NEG-INF:STAT-be.possible SENS-be
\l As for brothers' children, it is completely impossible for them to marry each other.' (140427 kWmdza stWnmW)

\t aʑo nɯ praʁwɯ rɟitpa ŋua tɕe , arɟit ni praʁwɯ rɟitpa kɯnɤ kɯɤrtsi ŋundʑi ,
\g 1SG DEM TOPO lineage be:FACT-1SG LNK 1SG.POSS-offspring DU TOPO lineage also SBJ:PCP-PASS-count be:FACT-DU
\l I am (Tshendzin) from the lineage of Praqwu, and [therefore] my two children also count as being from the lineage of Praqwu.' (140426 rJitpa)

\t tɯmu pɕoʁ nɯ tɤ́wɣrtsɯz tɕe , tɯmu pɕoʁ rɟitpa tukɯrtsi ŋu , tɯwa pɕoʁ partsɯznɯ tɕe , li tɯwa pɕoʁ rɟitpa nɯ pjɯrtsinɯ ɕti
\g GENR.POSS-mother side DEM AOR:UP-INV-count LNK GENR.POSS-mother side lineage IPFV:UP-GENR:S/O-count be:FACT GENR.POSS-father side DEM AOR:DOWN-count-PL LNK GENR.POSS-mother side lineage DEM IPFV:DOWN-count-PL be.AFF:FACT
\l When one counts from one's mother's side, one is counted as being from the lineage on one's mother's side, when people count from one's father's side (downwards), they count as being from one's father lineage.' (140426 rJitpa)

\t tɕe tɯrme nɯkɯɤmpʰɯmpʰri nɤ nɯkɯɤmpʰɯmpʰri nɯ rɟitpa tukɯti ŋu . apɯŋu tɕe , taʁrdo ra ɣɯ nɯrɟit nɯnɯ , ( . . .) tɤtɕɯ pɯnɯŋu , tɕʰeme pɯnɯŋu , tɯrme ɯkʰa zjɤkɯmɤtɕɯ , jɤkɯmɤrʑaβ , nɯra ɣɯ nɯrɟit nɯrɟit nɯrɟit kɯfse nɯkɯɤmpʰɯmpʰri nɯnɯra tɕe (taʁrdo) rɟitpa tukɯti ɲɯŋu .
\g LNK people AOR-SBJ:PCP-across.generations ADD AOR-SBJ:PCP-across.generations DEM lineage IPFV-GENR-say be:FACT IRR-IPFV-be LNK TOPO PL GEN 3PL.POSS-offspring DEM _ INDEF.POSS-son PST.IPFV-AUTO-be girl PST.IPFV-AUTO-be people 3SG.POSS-house TRAL-AOR-SBJ:PCP-adopted.as.son AOR-SBJ:PCP-marry DEM:PL GEN 3PL.POSS-offspring 3PL.POSS-offspring 3PL.POSS-offspring SBJ:PCP-be.like AOR-SBJ:PCP-across.generations DEM:PL LNK TOPO lineage IPFV-GENR-say SENS-be
\l People [related to each other] generation after generations are called a lineage. For instance, the children from Taqrdo, (…) male or female, whether they have left and been adopted as sons in someone else's household or have married away, their children's children's children, generation after generation, are called the lineage [of Taqrdo].' (140425 kWmdza08) <a href="https://doi.org/10.24397/pangloss-0003792"></fn>

\t tɯʑo tɕʰeme ɣɯ tɯrɟit nɯnɯ kɯ tɕe tɕe tɯwɤmɯ ra nɯrɟit nɯɕki tɕe li “arpɯ aɬaʁ" tutinɯ kɯra .
\g GENR girl GEN GENR.POSS-offspring DEM ERG LNK LNK GENR.POSS-brother PL 3PL.POSS-offspring 3PL.POSS-DAT LNK again 1SG.POSS-MB 1SG.POSS-MZ IPFV-say-PL INF:STAT-be.needed
\l One's children (EGO being a woman) call one's brother's children a-rpɯ `my mother's brother' or a-ɬaʁ `my mother's sister'. (140425 kWmdza01) <a href="https://doi.org/10.24397/pangloss-0003785"></fn>

\t nɤɲi ɣɯ ɯɣe kɯ tɕe tɕe , nɤj nɤɕki “arpɯ" tuti kɯra ɕti .
\g 2SG.POSS-FZ GEN 3SG.POSS-grandchild ERG LNK LNK 2SG 2SG.POSS-DAT 1SG.POSS-MB IPFV-say INF:STAT-be.needed be.AFF:FACT
\l Your father's sister's grandchildren have to call you `my mother's brother'.' (elicitation 2019-11-30)

\t iʑo jiwi nɯnɯ tsʰapa nɯkɯɣe pjɤŋu . ( . . .) aʑo tɤnɯkoŋtsoa ɯqʰu tɕe , tsʰapa juɕea tɕe , tsʰapa nɯ jikɯmdza ʁɟa ɲɯŋu tɕe , ( . . .) tɕe arpɯ aɬaʁ ntsɯ tukɯti ɲɯra ma nɯ<beifen> ɲɯmbro , ( . . .) tɤpɤtso kɯxtɕɯ~xtɕi ra kɯ nɯ apʰe “aftsa aftsa" tutinɯ , “arpɯ aɬaʁ" kɤti ɲɯra , tɕendɤre tutia kɯzgɤt ɲɯɕti ri nɯnɯ aʑo mɯ́jnɤxtʂaŋa
\g 1PL 1PL.POSS-grandmother DEM TOPO AOR:WEST-SBJ:PCP-come[II] IFR.IPFV-be _ 1SG AOR-work-1SG 3SG.POSS-after LNK TOPO IPFV-go-1SG LNK TOPO DEM 1PL.POSS-relative completely SENS-be LNK _ LNK 1SG.POSS-MB 1SG.POSS-MZ always IPFV-GENR-say SENS-be.needed LNK 3PL.POSS-age.rank SENS-be.high _ INDEF.POSS-child SBJ:PCP-EMPH~be.small PL ERG DEM 1SG.POSS-DAT 1SG.POSS-ZCh 1SG.POSS-ZCh IPFV-say-PL 1SG.POSS-MB 1SG.POSS-MZ INF-say SENS-be.needed LNK IPFV-say-1SG INF:STAT-be.needed SENS-be.AFF LNK DEM 1SG NEG:SENS-TROP-be.fair-1SG
\l [One of] our grandmothers was from Tshapa (…) After I started working, when I went to Tshapa, everybody there is a relative of ours, (…) I had to call all of them `my mother's brother, my mother's sister', because they are of higher 辈分bèifenage rank, (…) [even] small children called me `my sister's son', and I had to call them `my mother's brother, my mother's sister'. Although this was what I had to say, I found it unfair.' (2010-06)

\t ɯwi ɣɯ ɯwi nɯnɯ tsʰapa nɯtɕu nɯkɯɣe pjɤŋu tɕe tɕe nɯ ɣɯ ɯwi ɣɯ ɯwɤmɯ nɯnɯ ɣɯ ɯrɟit ɣɯ ɯrɟit ɣɯ ɯrɟit ɣɯ ɯrɟit kɯfse nɯnɯra nɯɕki tɕe tɕe “arpɯ nɤ aɬaʁ" ntsɯ tuti pjɤra . ( . . .) tʰam tɕe nɯra stʰɯci ɯkɯti maŋe , tɕe kɯxtɕi nɯra kɯnɤ “aftsa" kɤti ɲɯnɤzraʁnɯ qʰe “aβɣo" ra tunɯtinɯ , “api" ra tunɯtinɯ . tɕe tʰam tuotʂoʁloʁ ɕti . kɯɕɯŋgɯ apɯŋu tɕe nɯ tukɯti kɯra pjɤɕti nɤ .
\g 3SG.POSS-grandmother GEN 3SG.POSS-grandmother DEM TOPO DEM:LOC AOR:WEST-SBJ:PCP-come[III] IFR.IPFV-be LNK LNK DEM GEN 3SG.POSS-grandmother GEN 3SG.POSS-brother DEM GEN 3SG.POSS-offspring GEN 3SG.POSS-offspring GEN 3SG.POSS-offspring GEN 3SG.POSS-offspring SBJ:PCP-be.like DEM:PL 3PL.POSS-DAT LOC LNK 1SG.POSS-MB ADD 1SG.POSS-MZ always IPFV-say IPFV.IFR-be.needed _ now LNK DEM:LOC so.much 3SG.POSS-SBJ:PCP-say not.exist:SENS LNK SBJ:PCP-be.small DEM:PL also 1SG.POSS-ZCh INF-say SENS-be.ashamed-PL LNK 1SG.POSS-FB PL IPFV-AUTO-say-PL 1SG.POSS-elder.sibling PL IPFV-AUTO-say-PL LNK now IPFV-be.mixed be.AFF:FACT in.former.days IRR-IPFV-be LNK DEM IPFV-GENR-say INF:STAT-be.needed IFR.IPFV-be SFP
\l His grandmother's grandmother had come from Tshapa, and he had to call all of his grandmother's brother's children's children's children's children (etc) `my mother's brother, my mother's sister' (including small children)'. (…) Now no one says this any more, the young ones are ashamed of calling [elders] `my sister's child' and instead say `my father's brother' or `my elder sibling'. Now it is all mixed up, but in former times, one had to speak like that.' (140425 kWmdza07) <a href="https://doi.org/10.24397/pangloss-0003791"></fn>
